PREFACE
Tantra is a major development in the evolution of
Indian <span class="t0 t4 t6 t7 t8 t11 t14 t16 t17 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">spiritual</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t17 t18 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 hoverable">thought</span> inasmuch as it represents a
determined attempt at reconciling the apparent points of
conflict among the different schools of philosophy that
came up after the age of the Epics. Tantra seeks to
synthesize the monism of the Advaita with the dualism
of the Samkhya, enrich Jnana with the rasa of Bhakti,
join <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Nature</span> to her <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> in the <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> of the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span>
individual, harmonize the claims of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Spirit</span> with the
rights of Matter. It recovers the lost heritage of the
<span class="t21 hoverable">ancient</span> Veda which lays emphasis <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the commonalty
of man, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Nature</span> and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">God</span> and the equality of status
between Mother <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Earth</span> and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Father</span> Heaven. The principle
of Tantra is to reject nothing that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">God</span> has created, to
utilize every means to raise the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> to
the Divine. Unlike many of the older systems Tantra
is highly rational in its approach; it asks for no <span class="t7 t13 t19 t20 t29 hoverable">faith</span> in
advance. It is a self-verifying science of the development
of natural energies into their supernatural terms leading
to a cosmic enjoyment of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> in a <span class="t0 t4 t6 t7 t8 t11 t14 t16 t17 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">spiritual</span> consciousness.
In a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">word</span> it is the highway of mukti and bhukti in the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t9 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t22 t23 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">highest</span> sense.
The Kularnava is an important <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span> in one of the traditions of Tantra with a pronouncedly practical bent of
thought. It calls <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> to wake up to the rare
privilege that has been given to him, e.g. <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> birth in
which the being becomes conscious of himself and is
offered a choice: a choice between stagnation and rapid
progression towards his Godhead. He is warned of the
consequences of losing himself in the rounds of transient
excitements and pleasures He is also put on guard against
the many pseudo-paths that abound in this world. He is

viii

PREFACE

asked to purify himself and told how to do it. In unambiguous terms he is told that a wine-drinker is different
from the drinkers of ecstasy; the union of delight is
between the ascending Sakti and the presiding <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span>
above, and not between <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> and woman. In issuing
these warnings, the adepts of the Tantra <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> seem to
have anticipated the modern turn of mixing up sex with
spirituality. It is a pity that a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span> like this has not received
adequate publicity in the west where tantra-enthusiasts
are on the wrong track.
The Kulanarva prescribes the modes of preparation for
the <span class="t17 t29 hoverable">high</span> quest; it draws <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> ethics, religion, philosophy,
yoga to elevate <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> gradually to the level of godly
life. It comprehends the multiple personality of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> and
provides for the healthy growth of his mental faculties,
purification of his emotions and passions, orientation of
his <span class="t1 hoverable">physical</span> faculties through ritual, japa, mantra and
upasana. Who is fit for the path of Tantra? Who is
competent to guide the novice on the double-edged razor
path? What is the responsibility of a Guru to a
disciple? These and other relevant questions are raised
and answered in a satisfying manner.
An attempt has been made in the following selections
to present such contents as are eminently helpful to the
needs of the awakened <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> of today. Portions relating
to rituals, technicalities of special types of japa, etc. have
been kept out of the treatment so as not to tax the aspirant of the present times who has little <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> or energies
to devote himself to those practices, especially when it is
possible to achieve the same results by more psychological
means suited to the modern age and so elegantly presented in this text. Definitions of most of the important
concepts and terms in the Tantra Sastra, as given in the
text, will be found highly educative.
M. P. PANDIT

ARTHUR AVALON

INTRODUCTION
T h e Kularnava is a leading and perhaps the
foremost Tantra of the Kaula School. It enjoys
a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> reputation amongst <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t7 t10 t11 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">works</span> of its class and
as such is constantly cited as an authority. T h e
Chapters of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Text</span> here published n u m b e r
seventeen and the verses total 2058 according as
there are included or not vv. 123-144 in the tenth
Chapter. The Colophon however states that the
portion here printed is only the fifth part of the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">whole</span> T a n t r a consisting of 1,25,000 verses. T h u s
the Colophon of the first <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> runs - " E n d of
the first <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> being the first portion of the
fifth part entitled Urdhvamnaya Tantra of the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> Mystery and most excellent among
Agamas containing, 1,25,000 verses entitled the
Kularnava T a n t r a . " If this statement be correct
I have not on enquiry been able to discover the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">whole</span> work. Every Ms. which I have come
across contains the seventeen Chapters only here
printed. Either then the rest of the <span class="t6 t8 t10 t11 t16 t20 t21 t27 t28 hoverable">book</span> is lost
or possibly exists under some different names.
T h e Kaulavali which is a compendium by
Jnanananda Paramhamsa quotes <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> passages
as from the Kularnava which do not occur in
a n y of the <span class="t9 t12 t13 t25 hoverable">texts</span> consulted in the preparation of
the present volume. T h e <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">work</span> has been already
twice printed and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> not in the
ordinary course have found <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> in these <span class="t9 t12 t13 t25 hoverable">texts</span>
according to the original design of the publication. It was found however that the previous
editions of this and other Tantras w e r e in
general so incorrect that the present edition is

T h e Kularnava is w o r t h y of a close studyby those who <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> understand the tenets and
practices of the School of which it is a Shastra.
Having however regard to the <span class="t7 t12 t13 hoverable">fact</span> that it is
hoped to publish a translation of the entire <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span> I
have not <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t17 t18 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 hoverable">thought</span> it necessary to give such a
detailed analysis of the T a n t r a as in the absence
of such a translation it <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> have deserved. I
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> only here give such a s u m m a r y as
under the circumstances stated seems sufficient.
T h e first <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">chapter</span> opens with some fine verses
(vv. 1-121). Devi tells Shiva of how <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span> a r e
suffering and asks the means whereby they m a y
be liberated. Ishvara in reply speaks of the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and of the creatures who encircled by
Maya are like sparks of <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">fire</span> parts of him. Of
these m a n is the greatest. He is a self-killer
who having attained m a n ' s estate <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> seeks not
his t r u e good. " H e w h o does not cure himself
of the disease of Hell w h a t will he do when he
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> suffering from such disease goes to a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span>
w h e r e there is no m e d i c a m e n t ? " (v. 24). T h e
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> then dwells on the transitoriness of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span>
and of all <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> therein. " P r o s p e r i t y is like a
dream, youth is like a flower. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Life</span> is seen and
is then gone like lightning. How can anyone
w h o knows this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> r e m a i n content?" (v 30).
Moreover the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> of evils which arise

from attachment (v 55). Shiva says " O h Beloved
to sleep, to copulate, to <span class="t6 hoverable">eat</span> and other such functions are common to all animals. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Man</span> alone is
possessed of knowledge. He who is devoid of it
is a b e a s t " (v 69). Shun h i m who is addicted to
the pleasures of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> and who <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> boasts
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> knowledge. T h e r e are other impostors
also. Liberation is not to be got by m e r e l y
smearing oneself with ashes, feeding on husks
and water, exposure to heat and cold and the
like. "Donkeys and other animals go about
naked. Are they <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> Yogins?" (vv 79-86).
N o : then gain <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> and avoid idle
talk. What is the <span class="t1 hoverable">use</span> of Vedas, Agamas and
Puranas if one knows not the supreme <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> of
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> - (v 89)? " R e n o w n e d <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span> dispute among
themselves - some saying the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is ahead and
some that it is behind, others again say it is on
either side. Some say it is like this, others like
that " ( v 99). All such bewilder themselves w i t h
Scriptures and talk. T h e y lack realization
(Pratyakshagrahanam) (v 100). The Sastras a r e
n u m b e r l e s s : one should <span class="t0 t1 t8 t11 t15 t21 t23 t24 hoverable">master</span> their essential
t r u t h and then put t h e m aside just as he w h o
seeks the grain of paddy throws away the h u s k
and straw (v 103). Real <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> alone
liberates. Ritual and austerities are needful
only so <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> as the Real and the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> are not
known (v 113). Shiva concludes " W h a t is the
<span class="t1 hoverable">use</span> of many words? It is Kuladharma which
liberates. Beloved, I have spoken to <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Thee</span> in
brief of the creature and how he should l i v e "
(v 121).
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> II deals w i t h the greatness of Kulad h a r m a which Shiva has
extracted after
churning the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> ocean of the Vedas and

7

Agamas (v 10) and which excels all others as the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">light</span> of the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t14 t15 t16 t18 t19 t21 t22 t24 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Sun</span> surpasses that of the firefly (v 16).
The Yogi cannot enjoy; and he who enjoys
cannot know Yoga but in Kuladharma there is
both Bhoga and Yoga (v 23). But Kaula <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> can only be gained by one <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> is
pure and who has controlled his senses (v 33). In
v 84-85 Shiva says that the six philosophies a r e
the six limbs of Kula. T h e Kaula Shastras a r e
based on Veda. " T a s m a t vedatmakam shastrang
vidhi kaulatmakang priye (v 85)." Many however
being ignorant of the traditional teaching of
Kuladharma cheat <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">people</span> by their false <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> (v 116). Moreover the Kula path is <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> of
dangers (v 122). So also the Buddhist Vajrayana
is (I m a y add) compared to a hollow bamboo in
which a serpent is placed. It must go up at
peril of falling down. He who fails on this path
is l i k e l y to go to Hell. T h e Pashu should <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> avoid this method (v 124). Vv 140, 141 cite
authorities from Shruti (Rigveda) in support of
the doctrine taught.
T h e <span class="t26 hoverable">third</span> <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> treats of the Paraprasada
m a n t r a that is Hamsah which, as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span>
Cosmic Breath, pervades the world, opening (v 4)
with the assertion that Vedas, Puranas and other
Shastras m a y be preached abroad; whereas the
Shaiva and Shakta Agamas are mysteries (v 4).
V 10 refers to the four Amnayas or traditions,
some portions of which appear in the T a n t r a
Shastras. Urddhvamnaya is not to be learnt
by study of the Shastras but from its masters
(v30).
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> IV which is a difficult one deals w i t h
Mahashodhanyasa. F r o m it as <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span> as other
parts of the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">work</span> m a y be learnt how rigorous

the Sadhana is which is required of those w h o

T h e fifth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> treats of the greatness of
Kula. It contains a description of the Kaula
substances; the making of w i n e ; the various
kinds of w i n e ; its <span class="t1 hoverable">use</span> as Chitta-shodhanasadhana so that the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> m a y become Bramagah.
V 48 enumerates the fundamental doctrines of
this school that "success is attained by those
very <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> which lead to f a l l " (Yaireva patanang dravyaih siddhistaireva chodita). V 50
refers to animal sacrifice: and vv 67, 68 to the
necessity of wine and meat in the various forms
of <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> including the Buddha. V 90 Says
" A s soma has been ordained a Brahmana should
d r i n k ; " which other T a n t r a s are said to deny.
If this however be done in the ordinary a n i m a l
w a y even a Vira w i l l go to Hell (v. 93). Nectar
drinking is the union of Kundali Shakti w i t h
the Moonchit (Chichchandra). Others are but
w i n e drinkers (vv. 107-108). The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> meat eater
is he who has merged his Chitta in the Supreme
(v. 109). He who controls his senses and unites
t h e m with Atma is a fish-eater. The rest do but
k i l l animals (v. 110). T r u e sexual union is t h e
union of Para Shakti that is Kundali with A t m a ;
others do but have carnal connection w i t h
w o m e n (vv 111, 112).
T h e sixth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> deals with the characteristics of the worshipper, of <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> and purification of Kaula substances. Vv 37-46 deal w i t h
the lunar, solar, fiery Kalas orginating from the
vowels, the consonants Ka-kha to Tha-da and the
Yavarga respectively; the Kalas of Kavarga and
Chavarga, Tavarga, Thavarga, Pavarga and
Yavarga and Shavarga. Then follow several

mantras. Vv 63-67 give the Gurus. Yantra is

<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> <span class="t0 t4 t5 t8 t12 t13 t15 t18 t23 t24 t26 t28 hoverable">VII</span> describes <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> of Vatuka,

of mind. V. 99 contains the oft quoted <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span>
" D r i n k and drink a g a i n " which some erroneously suppose is an invitation to drunkenness:
notwithstanding the previous injunction and the
warning that he who disobeys it is likely to go
to Hell. T h e <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">verse</span> refers to Yoga " d r i n k i n g . "
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> <span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t21 t22 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">VIII</span> deals with the Chakra and the

is done is an <span class="t6 hoverable">offering</span> to Bhairava (v. 59).
Unmana is the <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> in which the Sadhaka is no
longer affected and Tata is the very self of the
Supreme Mantra (vv. 83-84), T h e states up to
Praudhanta are waking (Jagrat). Unmana is
is dreaming (Svapna). Anavastha is dreamless
sleep (Sushupti). The seventh Ullasa is Liberation (vv. 94, 95). (Turiyavastha).
Yoga is treated of in <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> IX. Advaita
doctrine in its <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> Aham Brahmasmi is accepted (v. 32). Jiva is Shiva and Shiva J i v a : the
only difference is that one is in bondage and the

" t h e Kulayogi behaves in such a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span>

h i m " (v. 4). But himself doing acts of kindness

The tenth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> treats of <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> on

Kulachara which should be carefully concealed
(v. 84). The twelfth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> treats of the Paduka
Mantra. V. 58 prohibits discussion with Atheists
or unbelievers in Veda (Nastika). The subject
of the Guru is dealt with at some length. T h e next
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> (XIII) continues the subject of Guru
(v. 41) and disciple (vv. 1-40) and their qualifications. Amongst other defective persons, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span>
w h o are lewd, given to drink and stupid are to
be rejected. The Guru should realise that he is
inseparate (avichhinna) that is one w i t h the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> which pervades the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">whole</span> universe
(vv. 67-68). V. 82 refers to the Lingas in the
bodily centres and v. 90 gives the eight bonds
(Pasha) which bind the Pashu. The Guru is he
who by destroying the pleasures of the senses
gives Brahman-Bliss (v. 97).
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> XIV deals with the testing (Pariksha)
of the qualifications of Guru and disciple; and
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> XV treats of Purashcharana and other
matters. Pranayama is dealt with (v. 35 et seq).
Vv. 65-69 mention the " d e f e c t s " of Mantras and
vv. 71-72 <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> the purificatory rites which
remove them. T h e various kinds of Mantras,
Siddha, Sadhya and the like are described. V. 96
classifies the letters according to the Mahabhutas.
When doing Japa a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> should control his

a n i m a l propensites, <span class="t6 hoverable">eat</span> sparingly, live hardly,
cultivate <span class="t7 t13 t19 t20 t29 hoverable">faith</span> and devotion and fix his <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> and
<span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t28 hoverable">heart</span> solely on " T h a t " (vv. 110-113). <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span>
XVI deals with rites done for the attainment of
various objects of desire. <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> XVII gives
the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> of a large n u m b e r of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">words</span> such as
Guru, Acharya, Deshika and so forth and contains a Dhyana of the Guru. At the end of the
seventeenth <span class="t0 t2 t3 t4 t5 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t20 t21 t23 t24 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">Chapter</span> there is a remarkable
<span class="t28 hoverable">passage</span> (v. 103) prohibiting (ordinary persons)
from reading the portions of this <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">work</span> dealing
with Asavollasa. This prohibition doubtless
has been prompted by the <span class="t0 t10 t11 t17 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">desire</span> that such persons should not be led astray and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> to
practices which might lead to their moral ruin.
For it is to be noted that according to the Shastra
the Rahasyapuja is not for all and any but for
such w h o m the Guru m a y consider qualified and
have been duly initiated. Except under the
conditions prescribed the Sadhana with wine
and so forth is prohibited and its accomplishment is admittedly harmful. But under the
conditions prescribed this Sadhana is said to be
the practical application of the principles of
Advaitavada which the Agamas of this school
teach.

CHAPTER I

<span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">HUMAN</span> BIRTH AND LIFE*
The Kularnava is the most frequently cited
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span> in the Tantra literature not only because
it is a leading authority on the Kaula Marga†
which is the most important and daring
formulation of the Shakta school of the Agamas,
but also because of its comprehensive sweep
which takes in all the fundamentals of the
Tantra Sadhana, its underlying philosophy and
its many implications, ethical and social.
<span class="t2 t11 t15 t19 t25 t27 hoverable">Written</span> in the simplest possible style - as indeed
all the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">great</span> agamas are - with telling
metaphors and imagery, incorporating many of
the gnomic passages in the Tantras, this <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">work</span>
of seventeen chapters consists of a little over
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> <span class="t6 hoverable">thousand</span> verses ranging over a wide variety
of topics but always stressing the practical side
of the agamic <span class="t7 t8 t12 hoverable">wisdom</span> and calling attention to
the urgency of following it in this very life.
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span> opens with a question by the Devi,

other <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> is useless. Mukti, Liberation, is

nor by the study of the Sastras; Jnana, real
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> alone can give the liberation.
Neither asramas (prescribed stages in life) nor
philosophies nor sciences can give the
deliverance; only Jnana can give it. And this
Jnana is received through the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Word</span> of the Guru.
All other w a y s are deceptive, oppressive; the
Truth-Knowledge alone is life-giving.
It is a star lighting an ignorant sea,
A lamp <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> our poop piercing the night.
As <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> grows <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Light</span> flames up from w i t h i n ;
It is a shining warrior in the mind,
An eagle of dreams in the divining heart,
An armour in the fight, a bow of God.
Then larger dawns arrive
Man's <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> becomes God's supernal Ray.
(Sri Aurobindo: Savitri X-3)

The supreme <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Knowledge</span> of the One declard
by the Lord, <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from ritual and austerity, is to
be received through the mouth of the Guru.
The <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Word</span> of the Guru, it must be noted, is the

Voice of the World-Teacher that speaks through

<span class="t3 t22 t28 hoverable">GLORY</span> OF KULA-DHARMA*
And what is Kula-Dharma?
Handed down from mouth to mouth in the
<span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> stretch of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">holy</span> tradition, the Doctrine of
Kaula is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t9 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t22 t23 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">highest</span> and the most guarded from
the profane and the unqualified. Seven are the
Ways for the liberation of man. The first is the
path of karma, the Vedic r i t u a l ; this is the
discipline for the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> of ordinary metal. T h e
second, <span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">higher</span> than the first, is the Vaishnava
path in which devotion to the Lord, bhakti, plays
a greater role than w o r k s and is meant for a
<span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">higher</span> competence. T h i r d , the Shaiva which is
m o r e a path of meditation and jnana, knowledge,
than anything else. These <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> orders or
successive stages of discipline are meant for the
o r d i n a r y category of seekers, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> a n y
special qualification, the pasu, creature w h o is
bound by the bonds of existence, pasa. T h e
fourth is the Dakshina, the path where k a r m a ,
bhakti, jnana are skilfully harmonised and
synthesised; the fruits of the first <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> a r e
organised and conserved. <span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">Higher</span> than the
Dakshina is the Varna, the reverse path w h e r e
the natural turn outwards, pravritti, is turned
inward, nivritti, to the source of all and everything in <span class="t0 t1 t5 t7 t9 t11 t12 t13 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t27 t29 hoverable">creation</span> is looked <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> and <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> as the
means for the return to the One <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">Consciousness</span>
that bases all and governs a l l . The process is one
of inner identification of oneself with the One

and explained by others.
For one's mind, one's
inclination and proclivity depend entirely <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span>
w h a t has gone before, w h a t has been prepared

External instruction is of little avail. T h e
<span class="t0 t2 t5 t13 t14 t16 t17 t20 t23 t24 t26 t28 t29 hoverable">second</span> factor is the degree of purification and
subtilisation of <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> that one has undergone as a result of japa, repetition of sacred

<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">GREAT</span> MANTRA*
<span class="t0 t28 hoverable">Eternal</span> and universal is the Lord. So is

Traditions, amnayas, sure means of liberation,

modes of expression suited to His different
moods of Being.
Facing the East was spoken the Purvaa m n a y a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> central <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is that of creation,
srsti, Path that of Mantra Yoga, and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span>
principles are twenty-four in number. Facing
South, was declared the Dakshina-amnaya
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> central <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> is the maintenance, sthiti,
of w h a t is created, Path that of Bhakti, and

North was declared the Uttara-amnaya <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span>

KULARNAVA TANTRA

Each Tradition has its own God-given
Mantras and sub-mantras leading to Enjoyment
and Liberation, bhukti and mukti. The fruit of
each Mantra is granted by the Deity presiding
over that Mantra. And all these Deities that are
adored and waited <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> a r e none else but the
emanations, portions of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> and his Spouse,
Ishwara and Devi. The t r u t h of all the Mantras
is known to the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Lord</span> alone and it is only out of
His grace that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> comes to know of it.
Any one of these * Four Amnayas is enough
to lead one to liberation. And if one were to
know all the four he <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> become the v e r y
Shiva himself. But <span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">higher</span> than all the four
Amnayas put <span class="t1 t2 t3 t4 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">together</span> is the Urdhvamnaya
which is so <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> because it is High, urdhvat
among all the dharmas, because it takes up, h i m
who is below, adhastah urdhvam, because it is
above the nether sea of samsara and because it
can be practised only in a <span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">higher</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of being,
<span class="t0 t1 t11 t12 t21 t25 hoverable">higher</span> <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of consciousness. It is the direct
single means for liberation, yielding a greater
fruit than all the other Amnayas, supreme.
" E v e n as I am to be adored above all others,"
bhairavi, Annapurnabhairavi, Panchami, Shodashi, Malini,
Valavala, with their rites and Mantras.
The sixth <span class="t3 hoverable">face</span> (Below) is lustrous of many colours and
concealed. It is by this mouth that I spoke of Devatasthana,
Asana, Yantra, Mala, Naivedya, Balidana, Sadhana,
Purascharana, Mantrasiddhi. It is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> Ishanamnaya."
(Sir John Woodroffe:
Shakti and Shakta)
According to the Niruttara Tantra, the Purva and
Dakshina Amnayas are meant for the Pashu sadhaka, the
Paschima Amnaya for both the Pashu and Vira, the Uttara
Amnaya for both the Vira and the Divya and the Urdhva
Amnaya is for the Divya.
* T h e Purva, Paschima, Dakshina and Uttara Amnayas,

says the Lord, " s o is the Urdhvamnaya to be

Vishnu among the Gods, Surya among the
luminaries, Kashi among places of pilgrimage,

One comes to it as a result of merit won in
several births. It is not to be known from Vedas
or Agamas or Sastras or Puranas, however
exhaustive they m a y be; neither by sacrifices,
nor austerities nor visits to pilgrim centres nor
even by means led by Mantras or herbs. It can
be known only through the mouth of the Guru.
Look for h i m , the Guru who knows all, fount of
compassion, endowed with a l l auspicious signs
who knows superbly the T r u t h of the Urdhvaamnaya, then from him receive the Knowledge.
Obtaining <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span> of the Urdhvamnaya from the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Word</span> of the Guru, you shall
attain liberation in this very <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> according to
the mode of the Scripture. You w i l l be blessed.
Where you live there shall reign Plenty, the
victory of Sri.

surpasses the very gods. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Though</span> he m a y do no

" W h o e v e r knows this Paraprasada Mantra,"

received through Initiation, he becomes Myself."
*'All these worlds, fourteen in number*, w i t h

CHAPTER IV

THE FIVE M'S AND THEIR
<span class="t10 t16 hoverable">FULL</span> SIGNIFICANCE*
The ingredients to be <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> in the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> of
the Devi a r e of many kinds. These comprise,
in the Kaulachara, madya, wine, mamsa, meat,
matsya, fish, mudra, grain, maithuna, woman,
<span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span> known as the Five M's, panca makaras
(each i t e m beginning with ma). The Sastra
prescribes in meticulous detail, the types of
vessels to be <span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> on different occasions, the
metal or substance of which they are made,
their dimensions; the several kinds of grain, the
proportion of their mixing and the manner of
their cooking; the preparation of different kinds
of wine from different substances according to
different formulas. Wine here is primarily
<span class="t0 t12 hoverable">used</span> as an agent for the release of the senses
from their engrossment in their outer objects.
The surface faculties and sensibilities constantly
exposed to the shocks and occupations of everyday <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> a r e temporarily suspended and the
deeper, the larger, the subliminal ranges of
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> are opened up making it easier
for the practicant to get a hold in the inner
recesses and <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">work</span> for the culture and the purification of the being. It is a means, says the
Kularnava, for the purification of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> and
consciousness,
cittasodhana-sadhana.
In its
fragrance is activated the icchasakti, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">power</span>
of will, in its taste is awakened the jnanasakti,

relaxation into the folds of a lighter and larger

Wine is not to be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> as wine nor <span class="t6 t20 hoverable">flesh</span> as

<span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Substance, and he w h o partakes is none
other than Bhairava himself, the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Enjoyer.
The bliss, Ananda that arises when all these
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">three</span> a r e fused in the <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> of the
practicant is real release, moksa. Ananda is the
intimate <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> and it is there
installed in each <span class="t22 t25 hoverable">individual</span> b o d y ; wine brings
out, releases into manifestation this indwelling
Bliss. T h i s is the <span class="t1 t11 t16 t20 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">reason</span> w h y yogins <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> in the
sanctified wine.
T h e r e a r e conditions to be fulfilled before

from all doubt, <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from fear, brave of spirit,
above dualities, above curiosity, one must have

<span class="t0 t4 t5 t10 t22 t25 t28 hoverable">person</span> alone the partaking of wine, processed
and sanctified by the charge of the Mantra,
awakens the <span class="t0 t1 t7 t12 t13 t14 t17 t23 t27 t28 hoverable">sense</span> of godhood which unties the
knots of life.

to be drunk. <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">Worship</span> the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Gods</span> and the Manes
in <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> accord with the prescribed <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> of the

before partaking of the meat and the wine.
Wine is to be received only for the benefit of the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Gods</span> who claim the Enjoyment and for steady4949 - 4

i n g t h e c o n t e m p l a t i o n o n t h e Divine, b y r e l e a s ing the m i n d from the tethers of the earth. He

be t a k e n f o r t h e flashing of t h e m e a n i n g of t h e

Wine, says another Tantra, should be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span>
only as <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> as the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> r e m a i n s merged in the

lays it down that wine is to be <span class="t2 t5 t11 t18 t19 t23 t26 hoverable">taken</span> only as

not affected. To drink more is to drink animally.
Completely <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from greed or <span class="t0 t10 t11 t17 t25 t28 t29 hoverable">desire</span> in

prasayet, make Her drink, not drink it yourself.
Partaking of these ingredients, says the Tantra,
at a n y other <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">time</span> except on this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t25 t27 t28 hoverable">holy</span> occasion
of dedication and <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> is condemnable.
Then, in a significant passage, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">text</span>
declares that just as the partaking of Soma is
enjoined <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> the <span class="t5 t8 hoverable">Wise</span> in the Sacrifices of the
Veda, so is Wine to be partaken on these
occasions (of worship), Wine that gives both
bliss and release. Now, Soma in the Vedic
context means, as all know, not merely the

In a crowning peroration of memorable

F r o m the Muladhara at the base go up again

only liquor.

CHAPTER V

REQUIREMENT OF WORSHIP*
It is not everyone who can <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">take</span> to the
<span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> of the Deity. To make offerings to the
Deity, to summon Her to accept what is
proffered, to receive Her in a fitting manner and
adore Her pleasingly, requires a preparation,
outer and inner, worked out in the present <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">life</span> or
the past. One who is so competent is fully
initiated, knows the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">truth</span> of the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">knowledge</span>
embodied in the Scripture. He is <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> of devotion
for the Guru, and for the Deity. And he has
control over himself, well-regulated in his life.
The mysteries of the Agamas, which are not all
openly declared in the Sastras, are known to
him. He is <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> of fervour for worship. <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">Worship</span> shall not be done as a routine or as a part
of discipline. He who <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">would</span> t r u l y <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span>
looks forward to the adoration with eagerness,
with joy. And when he worsh.ips he is alive
with the instruction of the Guru for it is the
Guru who puts him in contact w i t h the Deity and
to be conscious of his instruction is to enliven the
link forged by him. Pure of heart, superbly
joyous, devoid of anger and unsteadiness, rejecting the inferior ritual, cheerful of countenance,
he worships. He offers and adores with devotion.
Devotion does not come or grow in day. Even
when it is intense it does not last. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">True</span> and
lasting devotion sprouts after a <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> period of
self-effectuation and particularly by the Grace

of the Divine. It is then that offerings made
according to the instruction of the Guru, to the
accompaniment of proper Mantras, reach their
destination. It is then that the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> of the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Great</span> Sri Chakra, Abode of the mighty Puissance
of the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Mother, can be performed effectively by means of Mantra-Yoga. Not merely
chanting of Mantras, but by yoga of mantra
i.e. by a deep identification w i t h the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">soul</span> of
the Mantra that is repeated. Such worship, says
the Lord, He accepts with distinction along with
Her. And when the worshipper enters into the
Ritual, he must realise and come into a <span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> that feels divine. To t r u l y
commune with the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> and to offer oneself to
the Divine, one must become a w a r e of one's own
<span class="t0 t1 t10 t14 t21 t23 t25 t29 hoverable">state</span> of divinity. Such a worshipper attains
Fulfilment as <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">well</span> as Release.
<span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">Worship</span> must be performed in a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">place</span> which
is <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span> from distractions and disturbances, <span class="t1 t8 hoverable">free</span>
from crowd. The worshipper shall seat himself
in a happy position which gives stability to the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> and <span class="t3 hoverable">face</span> either east or north.
Prior to
beginning the ceremony he shall, with an unagitated mind, visualise himself seated in the
jewelled abode of the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Mother in the
Ocean of Immortality w i t h all the <span class="t17 t29 hoverable">high</span>
paraphernalia required for the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> and
perform the Puja according to the command of
the Guru.
Before proceeding to the worship, however,
there is an indispensable process of purification
which is fivefold in character; purification of
oneself, purification of the place, purification of
the materials used, purification of the Mantras
and purification of the Deity. Purification of

with sacred deference. The fraternity of the
Gurus † is to be invoked. And after sanctifying

the seat the Deity is called. She who dwells in
the cluster of Lotuses, Who is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> of
Causal Delight, ever active for the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">good</span> of all,
the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> Mother is fervently <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> into
coming and beseeched to stay as <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span> as the
<span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> is in progress. And the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> is
offered with an exclusive concentration.
T h e Divine, say the philosophies, is really
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> form, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> any features. Then how
is it, it m a y be asked, that It is enjoined to be
worshipped in so many kinds of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> and
lauded in Its features in the various scriptures?
The Agama gives the answer.
T h e <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is indeed the Immeasurable,
the Impersonal, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> attribute, a sheer
Consciousness. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Yet</span> for the benefit of the aspiring, of those who seek for It, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> assumes
forms, determines Itself in a <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">way</span> as to be
cognisable and accessible. It takes <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> but
certainly It is not limited by that <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> or any
<span class="t8 t21 t27 hoverable">number</span> of Forms. Thus, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> the Supreme
manavaugha, the <span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> order. T h e 6rst, the d i v i n e order,
consists of Adinatha and His Shakti, Sadasiva and h i s
consort, Ishwara and his consort, Rudra and his consort,
Vishnu and h i s beloved, Brahma and h i s w i f e - in a l l
twelve.
In the second, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">order</span> of t h e Siddhas - those w h o have
arrived at perfection and are e t e r n a l l y present and active are Sanaka, Sananda, Sanatana, Sanatkumara, Sanatsujata,
Ribhukshaja, Dattatreya, Raivataka, Vamadeva, Vyasa,
Shuka - e l e v e n of t h e m .
T h e third, the ordinary, is of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">gods</span> w h o apparently
occupy a subordinate position in this s c h e m e : Narasimha,
Mahesha, Bhaskara, Mahendra, Madhava, Vishnu - in a l l
six.
According to some other s c h o o l s , this manavaugha,
<span class="t0 t1 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">human</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">order</span> of Gurus, consists of the h u m a n Guru, Maha
Guru, Parama Guru, Parapara Guru etc.

REQUIREMENT OF <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">WORSHIP</span>

59

Deity is not determined or limited by Form,
She reveals Herself in m a n y forms. The
worshipper visualises the Formless One in
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> and adores Her in the linga, sign-symbol,
altar, Fire, Water, winnowing fan, wall, sheet,
Mandala (diagram), plank, in the <span class="t1 t4 t9 t16 hoverable">head</span> or in the
heart.
Just as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">though</span> milk is formed from the
constituents all over the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> of the cow, it
flows out only through the teats of its udder,
similarly the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> who is all pervading shines
specially resplendent in Images and the like.
The Presence of the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> is determined in its intensity by the appropriateness of
that Form, specially of the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> offered and
by the <span class="t7 t13 t19 t20 t29 hoverable">faith</span> of the worshipper. Cream, as <span class="t0 t1 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 hoverable">long</span>
as it lies in the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> of the cow, does not nourish
anyone. But when it is collected, treated and
used, it does promote nourishment. T h e <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span>
is likewise there spread in each b o d y ; but <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> proper adoration and evocation, upasana, it
does not yield fruit to man.
All the pranas of the Deity a r e to be summoned together, the limbs enlivened, all installed in the Image and then is the live Deity to be
worshipped. Otherwise <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> is fruitless.
There m a y be defect of Mantra, defect of ritual,
defect of process; still if this installation is
done in the proper manner, the <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> bears
fruit.
If there be transgression of r u l e there is no
fruit. Neither there should be allowed defect of
excess or defect of want. Only when <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">things</span> are
done according to the requirements laid down
that Japa, Homa, Puja etc. become acceptable to
the Deity and <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">therefore</span> fruitful.

60

KULARNAVA TANTRA

If <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> be offered <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> an active
<span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span> that the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> is there in the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of the Mantra and pervades through the
Mantra, it is useless. The Yantra is declared
to be ensouled by Mantra and the deity is in the
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> of Mantra. Worshipped in the Yantra,
She is indeed instantly pleased. And why is
this <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">form</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> yantra? Because it regulates,
subdues, niyantrana, all misery arising from
desire, anger and other failings. As the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span> is
to the jiva, soul, as oil is to the lamp, the
Yantra is the established seat of all the Deities.
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Therefore</span> draw the Yantra, meditate <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> Her
auspicious form, know everything from the
mouth of the Guru and <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> according to
rule. If <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> be done <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> proper Yantra
then it can only entail the curse of the Deity.
Each Deity is to be carefully installed in its own
Yantra and worshipped with all its paraphernalia. Should you be absent-minded, <span class="t8 t13 t21 hoverable">call</span> one
Deity and <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> another, you shall receive
the curses of both. Each Deity is to be received
with the honour that belongs" to it, with the
Mantra that is proper to its order. The inner
soul-force, antahsakti, shall be roused to its <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span>
potential and dedicated to the Deity through the
several movements of the worship.
It is only when all these requirements are
learnt from the Guru and <span class="t0 t5 t11 hoverable">worship</span> offered in
accordance with the rule, that the Deity is
pleased. The Puja must be <span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> in its limbs and
<span class="t10 t16 hoverable">full</span> in its duration.

CHAPTER VI

YOGA*
Yoga is the main process. T h e T a n t r a seeks
to weave it into every detail of life, give a
different <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t10 t12 t13 t14 t15 t17 t20 t21 t23 t24 t25 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">meaning</span> to each of man's activities by
making all of them means for the effectuation
and expression of the inner yoga of progression
from the h u m a n into the divine.
And of yoga, dhyana, meditation, is an
important l i m b . Dhyana is of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">two</span> kinds, gross
and subtle. When the meditation is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> a
Form, it is the gross, and when it is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span>
Form, the subtle. The grosser <span class="t23 hoverable">kind</span> of meditation with F o r m is resorted to when the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> is
very unsteady and needs to be given a prop, a
concrete <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> on which to fix itself so that it
may not wander away. But the <span class="t24 t25 hoverable">object</span> of both
the gross and subtle kinds of Dhyana is the
s a m e : steadiness, immobility of mind.
When the <span class="t0 t1 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Divine</span> is conceived with form,
it is contemplated <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> in its several limbs, feet,
<span class="t20 hoverable">hands</span> etc., in the prescribed manner. When
it is conceived as <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> form, it is contemplated <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">upon</span> as the Sacchidananda, allluminous, <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> parts. It neither rises nor
sets, neither waxes nor wanes, it shines by itself
and enshines others <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> effort. Infinite,
formed in Light, not perceivable to the eye but
simply existent, it can only be felt, become
aware of by the mind. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Knowledge</span> of That is
Brahman.

KULARNAVA TANTRA

And he <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> movement of life-breath
is arrested, who is immobile like the stone,
knowing only the supreme Self and Abode is
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the yogi who knows yoga. Where there
is not even awareness, w h e r e it is still like
blocked water, that Dhyana devoid of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Form</span> is
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> Samadhi. The Reality shines by itself,
not by mental thinking. And when the Reality
so shines on its own, one instantly becomes
That Itself. He who is as if asleep <span class="t0 t5 t8 t10 t14 t15 t21 t24 t28 hoverable">whether</span> in
the condition of dream or of waking, neither
breathing in nor breathing out, immobile, he is
t r u l y freed. <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Whose</span> senses a r e <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">without</span> stir,
<span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t11 t12 t13 t14 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">whose</span> <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">mind</span> and breath are absorbed in his self,
who is like one dead, he is <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">called</span> the Jivanmukta,
liberated while <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">yet</span> living. He neither hears nor
smells nor touches nor sees, neither he knows
pleasure and pain, neither he exercises the
mind. Like a log of wood, he cognises nothing
nor is a w a r e of anything; he is only absorbed in
Shiva, he is in samadhi. As w i t h <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">water</span> thrown
into water, milk into milk, ghee into ghee, no
difference remains, similarly no difference there
remains
between
the
jivatma and the
Paramatma, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">soul</span> and the Lord. Even as the
insect becomes a bee by force of concentration,
so can <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">man</span> become <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> by dint of samadhi.
And once the self is separated from the gunas,
it is never the same again, just as butter
extracted from milk even when thrown again
into the milk does not get into the old state.
Just as one in heavy darkness sees nothing,
so indeed the yogin sees not the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> which
does not hold his attention. This is the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">true</span> sign
of Dhyana: as one does not see the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> of
objects when the <span class="t2 t6 t19 t20 t26 t29 hoverable">eyes</span> are closed, so even when

YOGA

63

they are open, the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">world</span> is not seen. He who
knows the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t4 t5 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">Brahman</span> is aware of this worldmovement only in the manner of <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">men</span> being
conscious of some itching on their bodies.
Of him who has known the supreme Reality,
above forms, above change, the very Mantras
with their presiding Deities become the servitors.
Of him who is founded in the sole <span class="t0 t1 t13 t16 t24 t25 hoverable">consciousness</span>
of the Self, every movement is worship, each
utterance is verily a mantra, each gaze is
meditation.* When identification with the <span class="t0 t1 t2 t3 t4 t5 t6 t7 t8 t9 t10 t11 t12 t13 t14 t15 t16 t17 t18 t19 t20 t21 t22 t23 t24 t25 t26 t27 t28 t29 hoverable">body</span>
is gone and the supreme Self is known, wherever

By initiation, diksa, shall one be a Kaula,

obtained only by a happy ripening of previous
merit. The intensive practicant of the Kula
Dharma, howsoever low may be his station in
life, purifies instantly if only he is remembered or lauded or seen or bowed to or conversed
with.
